A.3 Dynamic Semantics 

The dynamic semantics is store-based. Evaluation runs a term against a heap . At runtime, term variables additionally range over heap locations 𝑙 : evaluation substitutes locations for bound variables. A configuration 𝐻 | 𝑡 pairs a heap 𝐻 with the term 𝑡 under evaluation. A heap is a finite map from locations to cells, 

𝐻 (𝑙 ) :: = 𝑣 | ref 𝑙 ′ | ref † 𝑙 ′,

a stored value 𝑣 , a live reference cell ref 𝑙 ′ holding the location 𝑙 ′, or a dead cell ref † 𝑙 ′ left by a deallocation. We write 𝐻 (𝑙 ) for lookup, dom (𝐻 ) for the set of allocated locations, and 𝐻 [𝑙 ↦ → 𝑐 ]

for the heap that extends or updates 𝐻 at 𝑙 . Each stored value also carries its footprint , the set of runtime capabilities it holds, which is the runtime image of its capture set; the parallel rules consult it and we leave it implicit. Both relations emit a trace 𝜏 , a finite sequence of heap events recording every access the run performs. An event is an access 𝜇 𝑙 , a read when 𝜇 = ro and a write when 𝜇 = 𝜖 , an allocation alloc 𝑙 ,or a deallocation dealloc 𝑙 . Traces are the objects over which the standardization and confluence theorems are stated (Appendix B.8). We write 𝜏 1 𝜏 2 for concatenation and omit the label on a step that emits the empty trace. 

A.3.1 Small-step Reduction. Figure A.6 defines the small-step relation 𝐻 | 𝑡 −→ 𝜏 𝐻 ′ | 𝑡 ′. An elimination form looks up its subject in the heap and reduces against the stored value. (s-app) ,

(s-tapp) , and (s-capp) apply a stored abstraction by substitution; type and capture arguments are computationally irrelevant, so these steps leave the heap and the trace untouched. (s-consumer) 

applies a consumer by unpacking its argument, reducing to a (unpack) redex, and (s-unwrap) opens a boxed value. The memory primitives are the only steps that touch the heap or the trace: (s-read) 

follows a reader to its cell and returns the stored location, emitting a read; (s-write) overwrites a live cell, emitting a write; (s-alloc) installs a fresh live cell and returns a pack of its location; and (s-drop) marks a cell dead. A let evaluates its bound term under (s-let) , then either lifts the resulting value to a fresh location (s-lift) or, when it is already a location, substitutes it (s-rename) ;

(s-unpack) substitutes the 𝑛 witnesses and the location of a pack. (s-par-l) and (s-par-r) interleave the two branches of a parallel composition and (s-par-join) returns unit once both are answers. A parallel node carries the footprints 𝐶 1 and 𝐶 2 of its two branches, the capture-set annotations of the 

(par) typing rule resolved to the runtime capabilities they hold. A footprint is a finite set of elements 

𝜇 𝑙 tagging a location 𝑙 with an access mode 𝜇 , and we order access modes by extending ro ⪯ 𝜖 with 

consume ⪯ consume , leaving consume incomparable to the mutabilities. A left step is allowed on two conditions. First, the emitted trace is authorized by the stepping branch’s footprint. Say a location 𝑙 is fresh at an event of 𝜏 when an earlier alloc 𝑙 event precedes it in 𝜏 . Then 𝜏 ⊳ 𝐶 1 holds when, for every event of 𝜏 whose location is not fresh at it, an access 𝜇 𝑙 has some 𝜇 ′ 𝑙 ∈ 𝐶 1 with 

𝜇 ⪯ 𝜇 ′, and a deallocation of 𝑙 has consume 𝑙 ∈ 𝐶 1. Second, the two footprints are non-interfering :

𝐶 1 ⊲⊳ 𝐶 2 holds when every 𝜇 1 𝑙 1 ∈ 𝐶 1 and 𝜇 2 𝑙 2 ∈ 𝐶 2 satisfy 𝑙 1 ≠ 𝑙 2 or 𝜇 1 = 𝜇 2 = ro . The stepping branch’s footprint then grows to 𝐶 ′ 

> 1

= 𝐶 1 ∪ { 𝜖 𝑙, consume 𝑙 | alloc 𝑙 occurs in 𝜏 }, adding the cells 𝑡 

allocates so a later step may use them. (s-par-r) is symmetric. These are exactly the obligations that the (par) typing rule establishes on 𝐶 1 and 𝐶 2, so a well-typed program never blocks on them. 

A.3.2 Big-step Evaluation. Figure A.7 defines the big-step relation 𝐻 | 𝑡 ⇓𝜏 𝐻 ′ | 𝑎 , evaluating 𝑡 

to an answer 𝑎 , a value or a location, while threading the heap and concatenating the traces of its subevaluations. It is the sequential counterpart of the small-step relation: values and locations evaluate to themselves (b-val) , (b-var) , the elimination forms evaluate the redex they expose, and 

(b-par) runs the two branches left to right rather than interleaving them. (b-let-val) and (b-let-var) sequence a let by evaluating the bound term first and then the body, lifting an intermediate 38 Xu et al.

B Metatheory of System CoreCapybara 

This appendix presents the semantic model behind Section 5 and states the theorems in the form in which they are mechanized. The Lean development is the ground truth. The definitions below transcribe it in the notation of Appendix A, omitting de Bruijn indices and well-scopedness side conditions. The model is a step-indexed Kripke logical relation over a higher-order store [2, 79]: types denote world-indexed predicates on heaps and terms, capture sets denote footprints, and the typing judgment asserts that the term evaluates to an answer satisfying its type’s predicate, with a trace authorized by its use set. B.1 Footprints 

A footprint is a capture set whose elements mention only heap locations (Section 4). Each stored value in the heap carries its footprint, the runtime image of its capture-set annotation, and a location inherits the footprint of what it names: 

fp (𝐻, 𝑙 ) =

(

{𝜖 𝑙 } if 𝐻 (𝑙 ) is a reference cell, 

𝑅 𝑣 if 𝐻 (𝑙 ) = 𝑣 with footprint 𝑅 𝑣 .

A semantic environment 𝜌 maps term variables to locations and capture variables to footprints; applying it to a capture set 𝐶 yields a ground set, whose footprint F J𝐶 K𝐻 𝜌 expands each element to the footprint of its location: 

F J{} K𝐻 𝜌 = {} , F J𝐶 1 ∪ 𝐶 2K𝐻 𝜌 = F J𝐶 1K𝐻 𝜌 ∪ F J𝐶 2K𝐻 𝜌 , F J{𝜇 𝑙 }K𝐻 𝜌 = 𝜇 fp (𝐻, 𝑙 ),

with mode application as in Appendix A. We drop the subscripts when the environment and heap are clear. A footprint 𝐶 covers an access 𝜇 𝑙 when 𝜇 ′ 𝑙 ∈ 𝐶 for some 𝜇 ⪯ 𝜇 ′. This is the reading used by trace authorization 𝜏 ⊳ 𝐶 (Section 4). Non-interference 𝐶 1 ⊲⊳ 𝐶 2 is as in Section 4, and two footprints are disjoint when they share no location at all. 

B.2 Worlds 

The denotations of the next subsection are Kripke: a type is interpreted relative to a world (Σ, 𝐻 ),the heap 𝐻 a program has reached together with a store typing Σ that assigns semantic contents to 40 Xu et al. 

its reference cells. As a program allocates and writes, the world grows, and denotations are stable under this growth, so a value keeps its type in every future world. The store typing is what breaks the circularity of the higher-order store: a cell typed Ref [𝑇 ]

should hold contents of type 𝑇 , but 𝑇 may itself mention reference types, and through type variables a cell may even store values of an abstract type. Σ therefore assigns each cell a relation rather than a syntactic type, and the relations are stratified by a step index 𝑘 :

World 𝑘 = Loc ⇀ Rel 𝑘 , Rel 𝑘 = Î𝑗 <𝑘 

 World 𝑗 → Heap → Term → Prop  .

A stored relation at index 𝑘 is a family, over every lower index 𝑗 < 𝑘 , of predicates on a world at index 𝑗 , a heap, and a term. The space of relations recurses on the index, so the store is inherently step-indexed. This shape is forced: a stored relation must be stable under world extension, and must agree with the content type in both directions so that writes can re-establish it. We write ⌊Σ⌋ 𝑗 

for the truncation of Σ to a lower index 𝑗 , which restricts each stored family to indices below 𝑗 .World extension (Σ′, 𝐻 ′) ⊒ ( Σ, 𝐻 ) holds when 𝐻 ′ evolves from 𝐻 , meaning every allocated location keeps its cell, where a stored value is unchanged and a reference cell may change its content and may die but not revive, and when Σ′ agrees with Σ on dom (Σ). A world is well-typed ,written Σ ⊩𝑘 𝐻 , when (1) every 𝑙 ∈ dom (Σ) is a reference cell of 𝐻 ;(2) every stored relation of Σ is stable under world extension, at every index below 𝑘 ; and (3) for every live cell 𝑙 ∈ dom (Σ) with 𝐻 (𝑙 ) = ref 𝑙 ′, the content satisfies its stored relation at every lower index: Σ(𝑙 )𝑗 (⌊ Σ⌋ 𝑗 , 𝐻, 𝑙 ′) for all 𝑗 < 𝑘 .Condition (3) exposes cell contents only at indices strictly below 𝑘 , so a read consumes one unit of the index. The model accordingly treats 𝑘 as a read budget : it bounds the number of read events of the runs about which the model makes claims. 

B.3 Interpretation of Types 

Types are interpreted relative to a semantic environment 𝜌 , which assigns to each variable of the context a semantic object of the matching kind: a heap location to a term variable, a footprint to a capture variable (Appendix B.1), and a denotation, a world-indexed predicate on answers, to a type variable. It is defined in Appendix B.5. The value denotation VJ𝑇 K𝜌 is then a world-indexed predicate on answers, defined by recursion on the type, mutually with the expression denotation of the next subsection. We write 𝑎 ∈ V J𝑇 K𝜌 (𝑘, Σ, 𝐻 ) when it holds of 𝑎 at the world. Because evaluation lifts values to the heap, an answer names a value either directly or through a location. and resolve (𝐻, 𝑙 ) is undefined when 𝑙 is unallocated or holds a reference cell. For a stored relation

B.4 The Expression Relation 

The expression denotation lifts a predicate on answers to a predicate on expressions: an expression inhabits it when it evaluates, by the big-step relation of Figure A.7, to an answer in the value denotation while accessing only the locations in its budget. The read budget guards every clause. Write |𝜏 |ro for the number of read events of a trace 𝜏 . Call a run of the small-step relation sequential 

when it follows the left-first schedule: (s-par-r) fires only when the left branch is already an answer, so the right branch of a parallel node steps only after the left has finished. This is the order in which 

(b-par) evaluates a parallel composition, so sequential runs are the small-step reading of the big-step relation. We write 𝐻 | 𝑡 ↠𝜏 𝐻 ′ | 𝑡 ′ for the reflexive-transitive closure of the small-step relation, concatenating traces, and ↠𝜏  

> seq

for its restriction to sequential runs. Then 𝑡 ∈ E J𝐸 K𝑅 𝜌 (𝑘, Σ, 𝐻 ) iff 

Σ ⊩𝑘 𝐻 implies all of: (1) Safety: every configuration reachable from 𝐻 | 𝑡 by a sequential run performing fewer than 

𝑘 reads is an answer or can step. (2) Postcondition: for every evaluation 𝐻 | 𝑡 ⇓𝜏 𝐻 ′ | 𝑎 with |𝜏 |ro < 𝑘 , the trace is authorized by the budget, 𝜏 ⊳ 𝑅 , and, where 𝑘 ′ = 𝑘 − | 𝜏 |ro , there is a store typing Σ′ at index 𝑘 ′ with 

(Σ′, 𝐻 ′) ⊒ (⌊ Σ⌋𝑘 ′ , 𝐻 ), Σ′ ⊩𝑘 ′ 𝐻 ′, 𝑎 ∈ V J𝐸 K𝜌 (𝑘 ′, Σ′, 𝐻 ′).

(3) Prefix safety: for every sequential run 𝐻 | 𝑡 ↠𝜏  

> seq

𝐻 ′′ | 𝑡 ′′ with |𝜏 |ro < 𝑘 , complete or not, the trace is authorized by the budget, 𝜏 ⊳ 𝑅 .Runs that exhaust the budget owe nothing. Adequacy below recovers unconditional claims by instantiating 𝑘 above the read count of any given run. When 𝐸 is an existential, the postcondition additionally requires the witnesses of the answer to be live in 𝐻 ′ and confined : every capability a witness reaches is either consumable under the budget 𝑅 or was freshly allocated by the run. This witness-confinement bound is what pays for the ownership lock of (unpack) (Remark C.2). The safety clause is a budget-indexed progress predicate. At a parallel node it is a rely-guarantee invariant: it carries the two branch footprints, requires every branch run to be authorized by its footprint and the two footprints to be non-interfering, and requires each branch to remain safe under every heap that runs of the other branch can produce. The postcondition constrains complete runs only, so prefix safety is what bounds the trace of a run still underway. In the mechanization, the sequential relation carries none of the guards of 

(s-par-l) and (s-par-r) , and prefix safety moreover realizes each within-budget run in guarded 

form, with the authorization and non-interference guards discharged at every parallel step. This realization is what embeds a run of the model into the full small-step relation, where the guards are checked at every step (Appendix B.7). 

B.5 Semantic Typing 

An environment 𝜌 realizes a context Γ at a world, written 𝜌 ∈ G JΓK(𝑘, Σ, 𝐻 ), when it interprets each binding as its denotation demands: 

• for 𝑥 : 𝑇 , the location 𝜌 (𝑥 ) is in VJ𝑇 K𝜌 (𝑘, Σ, 𝐻 );System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 43 

• for 𝑋 <: 𝑆 , the denotation 𝜌 (𝑋 ) is a proper, extension-stable predicate bounded by VJ𝑆 K𝜌 ;

• for 𝛼 𝑐 <: 𝐵 , the footprint of 𝜌 (𝑐 ) is consume -free and bounded by F J𝐵 K, and 𝜌 records the authority 𝛼 for 𝑐 ;

• for a lock [Ψ, Φ], 𝜌 satisfies [Ψ, Φ] semantically, as in the modal clause above. Consumption rights are carried by the binding authority, not by the footprint itself. The budget of a term that consumes 𝑐 acquires the consume capabilities through the rules that charge them. An environment is separation-well-formed when the footprints of distinct consumable capture variables are disjoint. Semantic typing quantifies over all realizing worlds: 𝐶 ; Γ |= 𝑡 : 𝐸 holds iff for all 𝜌 , 𝑘 , Σ, 𝐻 with 

𝜌 ∈ G JΓK(𝑘, Σ, 𝐻 ), 𝜌 separation-well-formed, and every cell of F J𝐶 K𝐻 𝜌 live in 𝐻 ,

where 𝑡𝜌 substitutes the environment into the term. 

B.6 The Fundamental Theorem 

Theorem B.1 (Fundamental theorem). If 𝐶 ; Γ ⊢ 𝑡 : 𝐸 , then 𝐶 ; Γ |= 𝑡 : 𝐸 .

The proof is by induction on the typing derivation, with one compatibility lemma per rule of Figure A.5. The auxiliary judgments of Appendix A have fundamental lemmas of their own, which the compatibility lemmas invoke. The two that carry the concurrency results are: 

Lemma B.2 (Subcapturing). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 <: 𝐶 2 and 𝜌 realizes Γ, then every capability of F J𝐶 1K is covered by F J𝐶 2K.

Lemma B.3 (Separation). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲⊳ 𝐶 2 and 𝜌 realizes Γ and is separation-well-formed, then 

F J𝐶 1K ⊲⊳ F J𝐶 2K.

Theorem B.3 is Theorem 5.5: syntactic separation denotes non-interference of footprints. It is what lets the compatibility lemma for (par) establish the rely–guarantee obligations of the safety predicate and the side conditions of (s-par-l) and (s-par-r) . Kinding has an analogous lemma: a capture set of kind ro denotes a footprint that covers no write. 

B.7 Adequacy 

Adequacy extracts unconditional statements about closed programs. A closed program is run on a 

platform of 𝑁 pre-allocated boolean cells: the context Γ𝑁 binds, per cell, a capture variable and a term variable of type Ref [Bool ]; the heap 𝐻 𝑁 allocates the 𝑁 live cells; and the environment 𝜌 𝑁 

maps each variable to its cell. The platform realizes Γ𝑁 at every index by construction, is separation-well-formed because all its capture variables are access-only, and is compatible with every footprint because all its cells are live. A program is a source term: it mentions no heap locations, so the platform configuration 𝐻 𝑁 | 𝑡𝜌 𝑁 is well-formed in the sense of Appendix B.8, as the substitution 

𝜌 𝑁 introduces only the live platform cells. 

Theorem B.4 (Seqential adeqacy). If 𝐶 ; Γ𝑁 |= 𝑡 : 𝐸 , then every configuration reachable from 

𝐻 𝑁 | 𝑡𝜌 𝑁 by a sequential run (Appendix B.4) is an answer or can step. 

Given a reachable configuration, instantiate the semantic typing at budget 𝑘 = |𝜏 |ro + 1 for the trace 𝜏 of the run that reaches it. The run is then strictly within budget and the safety clause applies. The schedule theorems of Appendix B.8 lift the statement to arbitrary interleavings. 

Theorem B.5 (Adeqacy). If 𝐶 ; Γ𝑁 |= 𝑡 : 𝐸 , then every configuration reachable from 𝐻 𝑁 | 𝑡𝜌 𝑁 by the small-step relation, under any schedule, is an answer or can step. 44 Xu et al. 

Let 𝐻 𝑁 | 𝑡𝜌 𝑁 ↠𝜏 1 𝐻 1 | 𝑡 1 and instantiate the semantic typing at budget 𝑘 = |𝜏 1 |ro + 1. The safety clause yields a maximal sequential run: one that reaches an answer within the budget, or one that performs at least 𝑘 reads. Prefix safety realizes it in guarded form (Appendix B.4), so it is also a run of the unrestricted relation. Confluence (Theorem B.8) joins the two runs. If the joining run out of 𝐻 1 | 𝑡 1 is nonempty, 𝑡 1 can step. If it is empty, the joined endpoints coincide. Then either 𝑡 1

is the sequential answer up to a renaming of locations, hence itself an answer, or the sequential run exhausted the budget, which condition (4) of confluence excludes: the joined traces have equal read counts, yet one performs fewer than 𝑘 reads and the other at least 𝑘 .Theorem 5.2 is Theorem B.5 composed with Theorem B.1, and Theorem 5.3 follows because the stuck configurations that adequacy excludes include every use-after-free and double-free: a dead cell matches no reduction rule (Appendix A). Adequacy also yields the guarantee behind the read-only mode: a computation whose budget is read-only cannot change the state it runs over. 

Theorem B.6 (Immutability). If 𝐶 ; Γ𝑁 |= 𝑡 : 𝐸 and the kind of 𝐶 is ro , then every run of 𝐻 𝑁 | 𝑡𝜌 𝑁 

to an answer, under any schedule, leaves every cell of 𝐻 𝑁 unchanged, in both content and liveness. 

The read-only kind rules out writes and deallocations, so both content and liveness are preserved. The schedule is arbitrary because standardization (Theorem B.7) converts an interleaved run to an answer into a sequential run with the same endpoints, to which the sequential argument applies. Theorem 5.4 is this theorem composed with Theorem B.1. 

B.8 Standardization and Confluence 

The remaining theorems relate the schedules of the small-step relation (Figure A.6). They are stated up to trace equivalence : two traces are equivalent when, at every location, they perform the same sequence of external accesses and deallocations, where events on cells the trace itself allocated are internal and do not count. It is the precise form of Theorem 5.6.

(3) 𝜋 (𝜏 1 𝜎 1) ≃ 𝜏 2 𝜎 2; and (4) |𝜏 1 𝜎 1 |ro = |𝜏 2 𝜎 2 |ro .

The renaming 𝜋 accounts for the free choice of fresh locations at allocation. In the mechanization, condition (2) holds up to the capture annotations on parallel nodes: their growth depends on the order of interleaving, but the footprints they denote agree. Condition (4) does not follow from (3): trace equivalence discounts events on cells the runs themselves allocate, so it alone does not pin down read counts. It is what closes the budget-exhaustion case of Theorem B.5. 

Corollary B.9 (Schedule determinism). If 𝑡 is well-formed in 𝐻 and 𝐻 | 𝑡 ↠𝜏 1 𝐻 1 | 𝑎 1 and 

𝐻 | 𝑡 ↠𝜏 2 𝐻 2 | 𝑎 2 with 𝑎 1, 𝑎 2 answers, then 𝐻 2 = 𝜋 𝐻 1, 𝑎 2 = 𝜋 𝑎 1, and 𝜋 𝜏 1 ≃ 𝜏 2 for some permutation 

𝜋 of locations. 

The corollary is immediate from Theorem B.8: answers do not reduce, so both closing runs are empty. It is the precise form of Theorem 5.7 and the operational content of data-race freedom: no observation of a well-typed program can depend on how its parallel compositions are scheduled. 

B.9 Mechanization 

The development is mechanized in Lean 4. All results are proved in full. The development contains no unproven obligations. The syntax, type system, and operational semantics are as in Appendix A. The model of Appendices B.1 to B.5 lives in the Denotation module, the compatibility lemmas and Theorem B.1 in Fundamental , the platform and adequacy theorems in Safety and SafetyReduce ,and the schedule theorems in Semantics . C Translating Capybara to CoreCapybara 

This appendix defines the type-preserving translation J·K from the surface calculus Capybara 

(Section 3) to the core calculus CoreCapybara (Appendix A), states its correctness theorem, and proves it. The translation is the bridge that transfers CoreCapybara ’s metatheory, soundness, memory safety, and data-race freedom, to Capybara .

C.1 Conventions 

We fix the following conventions, which the surface presentation of Section 3 leaves implicit. 

Root capabilities. The two special capture variables any and fresh are root capabilities . They dissolve into universal and existential capture quantification during translation. Recall from Sec-tion 3.2 that ⌊𝐶 ⌋ removes every root capability from 𝐶 ; call a capture set or type root-free when it mentions no root capability. All judgments of the translation are read over root-free sets: whenever a root capability would enter a capture position of a CoreCapybara type, the type translation has already consumed it into a bound capture variable. 46 Xu et al. 

Root-directedness. A well-formed surface type is root-directed : occurrences of any appear only as elements of the top-level capture set of a term-function domain, whose root-free part is access-only, and occurrences of fresh appear only in covariant (spine) positions, never in a function domain. The domain restriction on any is what (abs) and (app) already assume, read one arrow at a time: an any 

nested deeper inside a domain sits in the domain of a nested arrow, and that arrow quantifies it itself. The codomain restriction on fresh is a stated convention, enforced by the surface well-formedness judgment Γ ⊢ 𝑇 wf , which we assume. Under root-directedness each translated arrow binds a single 

capture variable 𝑐 ★ for the (at most one) any element of its domain’s top-level capture set, and a call instantiates 𝑐 ★ with one capture set, exactly as (abs) and (app) do with 𝑇 [any { {𝑐 }] and 

𝑇 [any { 𝐷 ].

Domain honesty. At every (app) and (consume-app) instance, with domain top-level capture set 𝐶 𝑇 and argument 𝑦 declared at capture set 𝐶 𝑦 , we require the argument to resolve onto the domain’s root-free captures: every root of ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋ is covered, at an equal or stronger mode, by a root of 𝐶 𝑦 (the covering order ⊑ of Appendix C.6). The domain’s root-free captures name capabilities the parameter actually holds, and the function body treats them as part of its footprint: it may assume them separate from what it captures, and the manufactured lock of Appendix C.3 records that assumption, to be paid at every call from the caller’s own knowledge of the argument. An argument whose capture set under-runs the domain would make the assumption unpayable at the call while keeping it vacuously true of the actual argument; we exclude such applications. A domain whose only capture is any , the common case in Section 2, satisfies the requirement trivially. 

Ambient contexts. The translation is stated for derivations whose ambient context, the prefix of 

Γ not introduced by a binder of the term under translation, declares term and type bindings only. Every capture variable of a translated context is then introduced by a translated binder and carries that binder’s lock or consume authority (Appendix C.4), which is what pays the fiat separations of (sep-root) (Theorem C.21). An ambient capture binding would arrive with neither, and a fiat separation between two such roots would have no translated image. 

Context-indexed types. The type translation resolves capture sets to their roots in the context where the type is read (Appendix C.3), so J𝑇 K carries a context index that we leave implicit. The index is stable: a resolution consults only the bindings of the variables the resolved set mentions, so extending the context disturbs nothing, and a translated type weakens to any extension of its context unchanged. 

Canonical derivations. The translation is defined on typing derivations, and the theorem asserts that the judgment translates, so we may choose which derivation to translate. We choose a canonical one, which keeps two sources of slack out of the translated obligations: gratuitously wide witnesses and gratuitously widened subjects. 

Definition C.1 (Canonical derivations). A derivation of 𝐶 ; Γ ⊢ 𝑡 : 𝑇 is canonical when: (1) (Tight witnesses) at every (app) and (consume-app) instance, the witness 𝐷 satisfies roots (Γ, 𝐷 ) ⊑ 

roots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑦 ) for the argument’s declared capture set 𝐶 𝑦 , and 𝐷 = {} when the domain men-tions no any ;(2) (Declared subjects) the subject premise of every elimination ( (app) , (consume-app) , (tapp) ,

(capp) ) concludes at the subject’s declared capturing type, up to subtyping applied inside covariant positions of its shape: in particular its top-level capture set and, for the function eliminations, the arrow’s capture annotation are the declared ones. 

Lemma C.2 (Canonicalization). Every derivable typing judgment has a canonical derivation. System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 47 

Proof. By induction on the derivation, rewriting each offending instance; the two clauses are established independently, and neither rewrite disturbs the conclusion judgment. 

(Declared subjects.) A subject premise is a (var) axiom followed by (sub) steps, collected into one step Γ ⊢ 𝑚 𝑆 𝑦 ∧𝐶 𝑦 <: 𝑚 𝑆 ∧𝐶 by (trans) . The elimination demands that 𝑆 be a function former, and 𝑆 𝑦 must be one of the same former: (tvar) only moves up to a declared bound, so a chain from a function shape to a function shape stays within the congruences. Inversion of (capt) and of the congruence ( (fun) , (tfun) , (cfun) ) splits the step into Γ ⊢ 𝐶 𝑦 <: 𝐶 , an identical domain (term domains are invariant under (fun) ) or a contravariant bound step, and a covariant codomain step under the binder. Re-associate: perform the elimination at the declared type, whose domain or bound premise the original premises already serve, and push the codomain step onto the conclusion 

by (sub) , using stability of subtyping under the elimination’s substitution, a routine property of the surface calculus. The use set is unchanged; for (capp) the charged witness 𝐷 is part of the term and also unchanged. 

(Tight witnesses.) If the domain mentions no any then 𝑇 [any { 𝐷 ′] = 𝑇 for every 𝐷 ′, and 

𝐷 ′ = {} satisfies access-onliness and separation by (ao-empty) , (sep-empty) , and (sep-symm) .Otherwise, by root-directedness the sole any sits in the domain’s top-level capture set 𝐶 𝑇 , so the argument premise contains the top-level subcapturing Γ ⊢ 𝐶 𝑦 <: ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋ ∪ 𝐷 and fixes everything below the top level. By the atomic decomposition of subcapturing (Theorem C.7), each atom of 𝐶 𝑦 

resolves, through declared capture sets, to atoms that are mode-covered by elements of ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋ ∪ 𝐷 .Let 𝐷 0 collect the intermediate atoms of that resolution that land in 𝐷 . Then: Γ ⊢ 𝐶 𝑦 <: ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋ ∪ 𝐷 0,by the same resolution with each landing atom kept in place; Γ ⊢ 𝐷 0 <: 𝐷 , since each collected atom is mode-covered by an element of 𝐷 ((sc-elem) , (sc-mode) ); and roots (Γ, 𝐷 0) ⊑ roots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑦 ),since each collected atom is a resolvent of an atom of 𝐶 𝑦 and resolution only multiplies modes (Theorem C.8). The rewritten instance uses witness 𝐷 0: the argument premise holds by the first fact, 

Γ ⊢ 𝐷 0 access-only by (ao-sc) from the second and the original Γ ⊢ 𝐷 access-only , the separation premise Γ ⊢ 𝐷 0 ⊲⊳ |𝐴 | by (sep-sc) from the second and the original premise, and for (consume-app) 

likewise Γ ⊢ 𝐷 0 consumable by (con-sc) . The result type [𝑧 := 𝑦 ]𝑈 does not mention 𝐷 , and for 

(consume-app) the charged 𝐷 0 ∪ consume 𝐷 0 lies below the original charge by the second fact, restored by (sub) . □

Translation on derivations. The translation is defined on canonical typing derivations , and is com-positional. The translated term inserts administrative forms, capture applications, locks and unlocks, packs and unpacks, that carry no source syntax but discharge the bookkeeping that CoreCapybara 

makes explicit. We write J·K for the translation of every syntactic class; context disambiguates. 

C.2 Translating Capture Sets, Bounds, and Permissions 

Capture sets. J𝐶 K acts elementwise, preserving variable names and access modes: 

J{𝜇 1 𝜃 1, . . . , 𝜇 𝑛 𝜃 𝑛 }K = {𝜇 1 𝜃 1, . . . , 𝜇 𝑛 𝜃 𝑛 } for root-free 𝜃 𝑖 .

Root capabilities never occur in a translated capture position; they are removed by ⌊·⌋ or turned into bound capture variables by the type translation. 

Mode application. Mode application commutes with translation. 

Lemma C.3 (Mode commutation). J𝜇 𝐶 K = 𝜇 J𝐶 K for every access mode 𝜇 and root-free capture set 𝐶 .

Proof. Immediate: both sides restamp each element of J𝐶 K with 𝜇 , and J·K preserves the under-lying captures. □48 Xu et al. 

Bounds. A surface capture bound is a capture set or a mutability. Capture sets translate as above. Mutabilities translate to the trivial core bound: 

J𝜖 K = ⊤, Jro K = ⊤.

A mutability bound carries no separation content of its own in CoreCapybara , where the trivial bound is ⊤. Its kinding force is recovered elsewhere: an ro bound additionally contributes a mode-context entry ({ 𝑐 } : ro ) to the lock manufactured at the binder that introduces 𝑐 (Appendix C.3), which is what lets (k-imm) pay the source uses of (k-imm) and (sb-kind) .

Permissions. Both systems qualify capturing types with a permission 𝑚 , and the translation carries it over verbatim: 

J𝑚 𝑆 ∧𝐶 K = 𝑚 J𝑆 K ∧ J𝐶 K, J𝑆 K = J𝑆 K (pure case) .

The permission is a qualifier on the capturing type , not an operation on its capture set: J𝐶 K is translated element-wise and 𝑚 never touches it. Every rule that reads or writes a permission does so through the type former: (var) preserves the binding’s qualifier on its refined singleton, (capt) keeps it rigid on both sides, (reader) introduces the read-only view of a reference at ro Ref [𝑇 ] ∧ {ro 𝑥 },and (read) demands an ro -qualified subject. Because (write) matches only the default qualifier, a reader-typed alias can never appear as the subject of a write: the qualifier plays exactly the role of the mechanization’s separate reader type constructor, which realizes the same distinction as a shape. Mode qualification of capture sets (ro 𝐶 , consume 𝐶 ) is an independent, element-wise operation used by charges and subcapturing ( (sc-ro) , (k-ro) ) and is likewise translated unchanged. 

C.3 Translating Types 

Type translation comes in two variants. The plain translation J𝑇 K is used in domains and other invariant or contravariant positions, where fresh never occurs (root-directedness). The result 

translation J𝑇 K∃ is used in covariant result positions, let-bound terms and function codomains, where fresh may occur; it closes the fresh occurrences into an existential: 

J𝑇 K∃ =

(

∃𝑐 1, . . . , 𝑐 𝑛 . J𝑇 ⟨fresh { {𝑐 1 }, . . . , {𝑐 𝑛 }⟩ K if 𝑇 mentions fresh ,

J𝑇 K otherwise ,

binding one capture variable per fresh occurrence, matching (let) . For root-free 𝑇 the two variants coincide. 

Plain translation. The base and capturing cases are homomorphic: 

J⊤K = ⊤, J𝑋 K = 𝑋, J𝑚 𝑆 ∧𝐶 K = 𝑚 J𝑆 K ∧ J𝐶 K.

Every function former, term, consumer, capture, and type function alike, manufactures a lock at its capturing type; their clauses follow the next definition.

for the root entry list of 𝑃 : one separation-context entry per capture variable, each collecting every access mode at which its variable occurs in 𝑃 . No two entries share a variable, so a lock built from System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 49

When 𝐵 = ro the parameter is bounded by ⊤ in the translated type ( Jro K = ⊤), and the mode entry restores that {𝑐 } has kind ro inside the codomain through (k-imm) ; a capture-set bound translates to the capture set itself and contributes no mode entry. The parameter entry {𝑐 } is not redundant: (cabs) charges the body at 𝐶 ∪ { 𝑐 }, so the body may pair 𝑐 against the roots of 𝐶 in its own separation premises, and the entry is what pays those pairs. The bound 𝐵 contributes nothing to Ψ𝐴 : locks record what the body assumes, and the body’s charge reaches 𝐵 only through 𝑐 itself. 

Type functions. Let 𝐴 = 𝑚 (∀[ 𝑋 <: 𝑆 ]𝑈 ) ∧𝐶 . The translation is 

J𝐴 K = 𝑚

A type binder introduces no root, so the lock has no parameter entry, only the pairwise entries of the annotation’s roots: a type-function body may still fire (sep-root) between two captured roots, and its lock is what pays for it. Correspondingly (tapp) carries no separation premise, and the translated type application discharges its unlock from the ambient pairwise separations alone (Appendix C.8): the surface rule and the manufactured lock ask for the same thing. 

Remark C.1 (Locks are shallow, root-level, and computed once). Three design points carry the appendix. First, locks are shallow : 𝑅 𝐴 reads only the arrow’s own annotation and domain, never the codomain’s spine. A separation that a nested body relies on lives in the lock of the nested arrow that abstracts it, is carried through substitution inside that arrow’s type, and is paid where that arrow is eliminated. The deep spine capture set |𝐴 | remains a surface device: the (app) premise checks the argument against it eagerly because surface fiat must be justified under instantiation, but no translated obligation ever mentions the deep part. Second, entries are root-level : each entry is the moded atom set of a single resolved root, so a body-level fiat pair is read off the lock by (sep-lock) 

directly, and a use site consumes an entry by resolving its own sets upward to roots (Theorem C.9) and descending by (sep-sc) ; no stored entry is ever projected downward, so no entry needs to carry a set together with its resolution. Third, entries are computed once, at the type former, and travel with the type as stored syntax: substitution acts on them componentwise (Theorem C.13), and widening the annotation re-relates them by (boxed-sat) (Theorem C.15). Stability under both is possible because term substitution does not touch capture variables and the domain of a term function is rigid under surface subtyping ( (fun) ). 

C.4 Translating Contexts 

Contexts translate pointwise: 

J∅K = ∅, JΓ, 𝑥 : 𝑇 K = JΓK, 𝑥 : J𝑇 K, JΓ, 𝑋 <: 𝑆 K = JΓK, 𝑋 <: J𝑆 K, JΓ, 𝛼 𝑐 <: 𝐵 K = JΓK, 𝛼 𝑐 <: J𝐵 K,

where the source consume mode 𝛼 ∈ { 𝜖, consume } maps to itself and J𝜖 K = Jro K = ⊤ on bounds. The manufactured locks do not live in JΓK globally. They enter the context only where the translated term pushes a lock, at a (lock) , (consumer) , or (unpack) binder. We write JΓK for the translated context interleaved with the frames pushed by the enclosing translated binders , and define it alongside the term translation. A source context extension contributes one frame per binder passed on the way from the ambient context to the site: 

• a term binder 𝜆 (𝛼 𝑥 : 𝑇 ) with arrow 𝐴 contributes 𝛼 𝑐 ★ <: ⊤, 𝑥 : J𝑇 ⟨any { {𝑐 ★}⟩ K, [Ψ𝐴 , Φ𝐴 ],where in the consume case the pair 𝑐 ★, 𝑥 is bound by a single (consumer) frame; 

• a capture binder 𝜆 [𝑐 <: 𝐵 ] with arrow 𝐴 contributes 𝜖 𝑐 <: J𝐵 K, [Ψ𝐴 , Φ𝐴 ];

• a type binder 𝜆 [𝑋 <: 𝑆 ] with arrow 𝐴 contributes 𝑋 <: J𝑆 K, [Ψ𝐴 , Φ𝐴 ];

• a root-free (let) contributes 𝑥 : J𝑇 K, and a fresh -carrying (let) contributes the (unpack) 

frame consume 𝑐 1 <: ⊤, . . . , consume 𝑐 𝑛 <: ⊤, [Ψ𝑤 , Φ𝑤 ], 𝑥 : J𝑇 ⟨fresh { {𝑐 1 }, . . . , {𝑐 𝑛 }⟩ K

with the ownership lock of (unpack) .System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 51 

The lock of each frame is available to every subderivation nested inside its binder, which is what makes the manufactured separations of Appendix C.3 usable in the body. The kill operators ⊖

that core (let) and (unpack) apply to their continuations are not part of JΓK: the main induction produces continuation derivations in the unkilled context and places them under the kill by Theorem C.24. 

C.5 Translating Terms

(readonly) , or (fresh) . The homomorphic and short cases are collected in the table below; the cases that insert nontrivial administrative structure are described in the paragraphs that follow.

where (reader) types ro 𝑥 at ro Ref [J𝑇 K] ∧ {ro 𝑥 } and the let charges the translated image {ro 𝑥 } of the source charge. Writes, deallocations, parallel compositions, and conditionals map to their core counterparts unchanged; their premises are the translated images of the source premises, using Theorem C.18 for the separation premise of (par) , whose payability hypothesis Theorem C.21 discharges at the site, and Theorem C.12 for the consumable premise of (dealloc) .

C.6 The Translation Theorem 

The consuming forms of the surface calculus charge the access of what they consume alongside its consumption, (fresh) and (consume-app) charging 𝐷 ∪ consume 𝐷 and (let) and (abs) bind-ing {𝑐, consume 𝑐 }, exactly as their translated images (pack) , (consumer-app) , (unpack) , and 

(consumer) do. The translated use set is therefore bounded by J𝐶 K itself. 

Theorem C.4 (Typability preservation). If 𝐶 ; Γ ⊢ 𝑡 : 𝑇 in Capybara , then the translation of a canonical derivation of it (Theorem C.2) yields a CoreCapybara term J𝑡 K with 

𝐶 ′; JΓK ⊢ J𝑡 K : J𝑇 K∃ for some 𝐶 ′ with roots (JΓK, 𝐶 ′) ⊑ roots (JΓK, J𝐶 K),

where JΓK is the lock-interleaved translated context of Appendix C.4 and J𝑇 K∃ the result translation of Appendix C.3. 

The side condition is stated at the level of roots. Write 𝑃 ⊑ 𝑃 ′ when every 𝜇 𝜃 ∈ 𝑃 has some 

𝜇 ′ 𝜃 ∈ 𝑃 ′ with 𝜇 ⪯ 𝜇 ′, extending the mutability order with consume ⪯ consume . This is a statement-level device only: it never appears as the premise of a separation rule (a variable’s runtime footprint can strictly under-run its root, so root covering does not transport separation). Eager surface charging and lazy core charging differ exactly below variable resolution: the surface charges a variable occurrence {𝑥 } eagerly, while the core charges its uses at eliminations, but {𝑥 }

and the declared capture set it resolves to have the same roots, so the two agree once resolved. The consumers of the theorem, the core access-only, consumable, and accessible predicates and the kill operation, are themselves root-based, so the root-level bound is exactly what they need. The proof is in Appendix C.8, by induction on the canonical source derivation, one case per rule, using the lemma stack of Appendix C.7. Because the translated term is typed against J𝑇 K

and its uses are root-covered by J𝐶 K, and CoreCapybara ’s dynamic semantics preserves both, the metatheory of Section 5 transfers to Capybara .

Corollary C.5 (Transfer of guarantees). A well-typed Capybara program enjoys type sound-ness (Theorem 5.2), memory safety (Theorem 5.3), and data-race freedom (Theorem 5.5, Theorem 5.7). 

Proof. By Theorem C.4 the translation of the program is a well-typed CoreCapybara program, to which the theorems of Section 5 apply. The surface constructs take their operational meaning through the translation (Section 3.4), so the guarantees, which are stated over the traces and final memories of CoreCapybara runs, are statements about the program’s own runs. The administrative forms the translation inserts do not disturb them: capture applications, type applications, appli-cations of the inserted lambdas, locks, unlocks, packs and unpacks reduce by (s-capp) , (s-tapp) ,

(s-app) , (s-unwrap) , and (s-unpack) , each of which leaves the heap and the trace untouched, so every heap event of a run belongs to a source construct. □

C.7 Lemma Stack 

The proof of Theorem C.4 rests on the following lemmas. Except where noted, each is by induction on the indicated derivation. 54 Xu et al. 

L1: Mode monotonicity. Theorem C.3 already records J𝜇 𝐶 K = 𝜇 J𝐶 K. We add monotonicity of qualification. 

Lemma C.6 (Qualification monotonicity). If JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 1K <: J𝐶 2K then JΓK ⊢ 𝜇 J𝐶 1K <:

𝜇 J𝐶 2K for every 𝜇 .

Proof. For 𝜇 = 𝜖 this is the hypothesis. For 𝜇 = ro it is (sc-ro-mono) ; for 𝜇 = consume it is 

(sc-consume-mono) . □

L2: Roots. Root resolution (Appendix A) underlies the lock manufacture, and four of its properties recur. Throughout, ⊑ is the covering order of Appendix C.6, and we use silently that resolution is multiplicative, roots (Γ, 𝜇 𝐶 ) = 𝜇 roots (Γ, 𝐶 ), and distributes over union, both immediate from its definition, and that it commutes with the translation, roots (JΓK, J𝐶 K) = Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 )K for root-free 

𝐶 , since the translation preserves every binding’s capture set elementwise and the interleaved frames bind no term variables that 𝐶 mentions. 

Lemma C.7 (Atomic decomposition). Say an atom 𝜇 𝜃 lands in 𝐶 2 over Γ when either (i) some 

𝜇 ′ 𝜃 ∈ 𝐶 2 with 𝜇 ⪯ 𝜇 ′ (extending the mutability order with consume ⪯ consume ), or (ii) 𝜃 is a term variable 𝑥 : 𝑚 𝑆 ∧ 𝐶 𝑥 ∈ Γ, 𝜇 is a mutability, and every atom of 𝜇 𝐶 𝑥 lands in 𝐶 2. Then Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 <: 𝐶 2

holds if and only if every atom of 𝐶 1 lands in 𝐶 2.

Proof. (⇐) Per atom: clause (i) is (sc-elem) after (sc-mode) (for consume atoms the covering mode is equal, so (sc-elem) alone); clause (ii) is (sc-var) qualified by (sc-ro-mono) when 𝜇 = ro ,followed by (sc-trans) on the inner landings; (sc-union) assembles the atoms. ( ⇒) By induction on the subcapturing derivation, using two closure properties of landing, each by induction on the landing derivation: landing composes (an atom landing in 𝐶 2 lands in 𝐶 3 whenever every atom of 

𝐶 2 does), and landing is stable under qualification (if 𝜇 𝜃 lands in 𝐶 2 then 𝜇 ′ (𝜇 𝜃 ) lands in 𝜇 ′𝐶 2). 

(sc-elem) and (sc-var) are landing axioms, (sc-mode) and (sc-ro-mono) use stability, (sc-trans) 

uses composition, and (sc-union) splits. □

Lemma C.8 (Root monotonicity). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 <: 𝐶 2 then roots (Γ, 𝐶 1) ⊑ roots (Γ, 𝐶 2).

Proof. By induction on the derivation. (sc-elem) : containment of atoms gives containment of their resolutions. (sc-var) : roots (Γ, {𝑥 }) = roots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑥 ) by definition, so the two sides are equal. 

(sc-mode) and (sc-ro-mono) : multiplicativity, with the covering mode weakened by ⪯. (sc-union) :resolution distributes. (sc-trans) : ⊑ is transitive. □

over Γ.

by Theorem C.6, then (sc-trans) with the inductive Γ ⊢ 𝜇 𝐶 𝑥 <: roots (Γ, 𝜇 𝐶 𝑥 ) and multiplicativity. 

(sc-union) assembles. □

L3: Subcapturing preservation.

L4: Capability kinding, access-only, consumable, accessible. 

Lemma C.12 (Predicate preservation). Each surface predicate implies its core image: Γ ⊢ 𝐶 :

𝑚 ⇒ JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 K : 𝑚 ; Γ ⊢ 𝐶 access-only ⇒ JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 K access-only ; and Γ ⊢ 𝐶 consumable ⇒

(ao-sc) uses Theorem C.11 together with Theorem C.8 read in the core: shrinking a set covers its roots, and neither predicate can acquire a consume mark or a non-consume binding by shrinking. The accessible predicate is preserved likewise: the translated roots carry no killed binding because the source context has no killed variables and the translated kills are introduced only where the source (let) consumes, tracked by Theorem C.24. □

L5: Substitution and instantiation. The translated eliminations substitute a term variable, a type, or a capture set into a translated type. Away from the manufactured locks and codomain annotations, translation and substitution commute on the nose; at the locks, substitution replaces the resolved entries by written-level sets, and one subtyping cast re-relates the two. 

Lemma C.13 (Substitution commutation). J[𝑋 := 𝑆 ]𝑈 K = [𝑋 := J𝑆 K]J𝑈 K, and likewise for J·K∃ :type substitution touches no capture set. For term and capture substitution, J·K and the substitution agree on every position except the stored entries Ψ𝐴 and annotations 𝑊 𝐴 of function types: domains, outer capture sets, and all other capture positions are translated elementwise, where [𝑧 := 𝑦 ]J𝐶 K =

J[𝑧 := 𝑦 ]𝐶 K and [𝑐 := J𝐷 K]J𝐶 K = J[𝑐 := 𝐷 ]𝐶 K hold by definition. On a stored entry, substitution acts componentwise: a term substitution is the identity (entries contain only capture variables), and a capture substitution [𝑐 := J𝐷 K] replaces the atoms of the entry 𝑃 |𝑐 by the correspondingly qualified 

J𝐷 K and leaves the other entries unchanged. 

Proof. By induction on the type. Entries and annotations are stored root sets (Appendix C.3); term variables do not occur in them, and a capture substitution acts on capture sets elementwise by definition. □56 Xu et al.

Proof. For (tapp) the two sides are equal by Theorem C.13. For the others, by induction on 𝑈 ; all positions except modal wrappers and annotations agree on the nose by Theorem C.13 (in particular every domain, which is invariant, mentions the substituted variables only in elementwise-translated capture sets). At an annotation, the substituted 𝜎𝑊 and the re-resolved 𝑊 ′ are related by 𝐾 ⊢ 𝜎𝑊 <:

Covering lifts to subcapturing elementwise ( (sc-elem) , (sc-mode) ,

(sc-union) ). At a modal wrapper, split by (trans) into (boxed) (the inductive hypothesis under the shared lock) and (boxed-sat) , whose obligation asks each entry pair of the substituted 𝜎 Ψ to be separated under [Ψ′] and each 𝜎 Φ entry to be kinded. A pair of unsubstituted entries is a pair of single-variable root entries whose variables also carry entries in Ψ′ at covering modes, so 

(sep-lock) and (sep-sc) close it. A pair involving the substituted entry 𝜇 J𝐷 K resolves upward by Theorem C.9; each of its root atoms is covered by an entry variable of Ψ′ (tightness and domain honesty for (app) , the charged witness for (capp) ), so (sep-lock) pairs it with the other entry’s variable, (sep-union) assembles the atoms, and (sep-sc) descends to the entries. A 𝜎 Φ entry is either preserved in Φ′ ((k-imm) ) or, when the substitution instantiated its variable, kinded through Theorem C.12 exactly as in the (cfun) case of Theorem C.15. □

L6: Subtyping preservation. 

Lemma C.15 (Subtyping preservation). If Γ ⊢ 𝑇 1 <: 𝑇 2 then JΓK ⊢ J𝑇 1K∃ <: J𝑇 2K∃ .

(capt) :the IH and Theorem C.11 feed (capt) , which carries the permission 𝑚 rigidly on both sides exactly as the source rule does. Γ ⊢ (∀( 𝑥 : 𝑇 )𝑈 1) ∧𝐶 1 <: (∀( 𝑥 : 𝑇 )𝑈 2) ∧𝐶 2

from Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 <: 𝐶 2 and (Γ, 𝑥 : 𝑇 ) ⊢ 𝑈 1 <: 𝑈 2. The translated shapes share the binder prefix 

∀[ 𝑐 ★ <: ⊤]∀( 𝑥 : J𝑇 ⟨any { {𝑐 ★}⟩ K) on the nose, so (cfun) (bounds ⊤, (sb-top) ) and (fun) (domain by (refl) ) reduce the claim to the codomains, two capturing modal types. Their (capt) splits into the annotation step and the modal step. Annotation: 𝑅 𝐴 1 ⊑ 𝑅 𝐴 2 by Theorem C.8 on Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 <: 𝐶 2

L7: Separation. The surface leaf (sep-root) separates any two distinct roots by fiat; the core has no fiat, and the translation pays every pair from a lock, from consume authority, or from read-only kinding. The next lemma extracts from a surface separation everything the payment needs, the following definition names the payments, and the preservation lemma reconstructs the core derivation; which payments are available at a site is the business of Theorem C.21. 

Lemma C.16 (Root characterization). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲⊳ 𝐶 2, then for every pair of atoms 𝜇 𝑝 ∈

roots (Γ, 𝐶 1) and 𝜈 𝑞 ∈ roots (Γ, 𝐶 2): either 𝑝 ≠ 𝑞 , or both atoms are read-only in the sense of Theo-rem C.10. The same holds for Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 # 𝐶 2 with the second alternative dropped, and for Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲ 𝐶 2

restricted to the consume -marked atoms of roots (Γ, 𝐶 1): a consumed root of 𝐶 1 is not a root of 𝐶 2.

Proof. By induction on the respective derivation. (sep-empty) is vacuous; (sep-symm) and (sep-union) preserve the condition (it is symmetric and resolution distributes). (sep-root) : the two sides resolve to the two distinct atoms. (sep-ro) : by Theorem C.10 on its kinding and access-only premises, every atom of both resolutions is read-only. (sep-sc) : Theorem C.8 covers each atom of the shrunken side at a weaker mode, and both alternatives are closed downward under ⪯ (a 

consume atom is covered only by a consume atom). Disjointness drops (sep-ro) , and with it the second alternative. For sequential composition: (seq-access-only) has no consume -marked atom in roots (Γ, 𝐶 1) by definition of access-only; (seq-sep) defers to the separation claim, whose second alternative is unavailable to a consume -marked atom; (seq-sc) uses Theorem C.8 as above; 

(seq-union) splits. □

Definition C.17 (Payable pairs). In a core context 𝐾 , a pair of atoms 𝜇 𝑝 , 𝜈 𝑞 over distinct capture variables 𝑝 ≠ 𝑞 is payable when 𝐾 ⊢ { 𝜇 𝑝 } ⊲⊳ {𝜈 𝑞 } is derivable. A set of atoms is pairwise payable 

when all its distinct-variable pairs are. Payability is closed under context extension (derivations weaken), under kills that touch neither variable (Theorem C.24), and under mode weakening: if the pair at (𝜇 ′, 𝜈 ′) is payable and 𝜇 ⪯ 𝜇 ′, 𝜈 ⪯ 𝜈 ′, then so is the pair at (𝜇, 𝜈 ), by (sep-sc) and (sc-mode) 

on both sides. 

Lemma C.18 (Separation preservation). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲⊳ 𝐶 2 and every distinct-variable pair of atoms of Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 1)K × Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 2)K is payable in JΓK, then JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 1K ⊲⊳ J𝐶 2K.

Proof. Write 𝑃 𝑖 = Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑖 )K = roots (JΓK, J𝐶 𝑖 K). First derive ⊢ 𝑃 1 ⊲⊳ 𝑃 2 atom by atom: a distinct-variable pair is payable by hypothesis; a shared-variable pair is read-only on both sides by Theorem C.16, and (sep-ro) separates the two singletons, whose access-only premises hold because a read-only atom is not consume -marked, and whose kinding premises hold by (k-ro) 

for an ro -marked atom and by (k-imm) for an ro -bounded one, reading the Φ entry of the binder’s frame (Appendix C.2). (sep-union) and (sep-symm) assemble the atoms into ⊢ 𝑃 1 ⊲⊳ 𝑃 2. Finally 

(sep-sc) on both sides (through (sep-symm) ) descends along ⊢ J𝐶 𝑖 K <: 𝑃 𝑖 (Theorem C.9). □58 Xu et al. 

Corollary C.19 (Disjointness preservation). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 # 𝐶 2, Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 consumable , and Γ ⊢

𝐶 2 consumable , then JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 1K # J𝐶 2K.

Proof. By Theorem C.16 (disjointness clause) the two root sets share no variable, and by Theorem C.12 all their variables are consume -bound in JΓK. (sep-consumable) separates each pair at its stated modes, staying inside the disjointness fragment; (sep-union) , (sep-symm) , and 

(sep-sc) along Theorem C.9 assemble and descend as in Theorem C.18. No lock and no read-only leaf is consulted. □

L8: Sequential composition. 

Lemma C.20 (Seqential composition preservation). If Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲ 𝐶 2 and every distinct-variable pair of a consume -marked atom of Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 1)K with an atom of Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 2)K is payable in JΓK,then JΓK ⊢ J𝐶 1K ⊲ J𝐶 2K.

Proof. By reconstruction, not by induction on the source derivation. (seq-sc) traces J𝐶 1K up to 

𝑃 1 = Jroots (Γ, 𝐶 1)K (Theorem C.9), and (seq-union) splits 𝑃 1 into atoms. An atom without consume 

mark is access-only, so (seq-access-only) closes it. A consume -marked atom consume 𝑝 is, by Theorem C.16, over a variable that is not a variable of roots (Γ, 𝐶 2), so all its pairs with the atoms of 

𝑃 2 are distinct-variable and payable by hypothesis; assembling them by (sep-union) /(sep-symm) and descending to J𝐶 2K by (sep-sc) gives ⊢ { consume 𝑝 } ⊲⊳ J𝐶 2K, and (seq-sep) closes the atom. □

L9: The ambient invariant. The payability hypotheses of Theorems C.18 and C.20 are discharged uniformly: at every site of the main induction, the roots of the site’s own charge and witnesses are pairwise payable. This is the translated image of (sep-root) ’s fiat, cut down from all pairs of roots in scope to the pairs the site can actually mention. A site of a canonical derivation is a subderivation occurrence; its site root set 𝜌 (𝑠 ) is roots (Γ𝑠 , 𝐶 𝑠 )

for its context Γ𝑠 and use set 𝐶 𝑠 , together with roots (Γ𝑠 , 𝐷 ) for the witnesses 𝐷 of its own (app) and 

(consume-app) premises ( (capp) witnesses are already charged). 

Lemma C.21 (Ambient invariant). At every site 𝑠 of a canonical source derivation under the ambient convention, J𝜌 (𝑠 )K is pairwise payable in the site’s translated context JΓ𝑠 K.

Proof. By induction on the path from the derivation’s root to 𝑠 , using the closure of payability under context extension and mode weakening (Theorem C.17). 

Root. The ambient context declares no capture variables, so every resolution over it is empty and 

𝜌 is empty. 

Descending within a rule instance. Every premise’s use set is a subset of the conclusion’s, equal to it, or below it in subcapturing ( (sub) ), so Theorem C.8 covers the premise’s roots by the conclusion’s at weaker modes, and mode closure transfers payability. Witnesses stay inside 𝜌 : an (app) witness is tight, roots (Γ, 𝐷 ) ⊑ roots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑦 ) = roots (Γ, {𝑦 }) (Theorem C.1), and (consume-app) and (capp) 

charge their witnesses outright. 

Crossing an abstraction binder. Here the invariant is re-established wholesale by the binder’s own lock, with no help from the enclosing site. For a term binder with arrow 𝐴 , the body’s use set is 

𝐶 ∪ { 𝑥 } (plus {𝑐 ★, consume 𝑐 ★} in the consume case), and 

roots (Γ′, 𝐶 ∪ { 𝑥 }) = roots (Γ, ⌊𝐶 ⌋) ∪ { 𝑐 ★-atoms } ∪ roots (Γ, ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋) = 𝑅 𝐴 ∪ { 𝑐 ★-atoms },

since {𝑥 } resolves through its declared J𝑇 ⟨any { {𝑐 ★}⟩ K. Every atom of the body’s site root set therefore lies, at its occurring mode, in an entry of Ψ𝐴 : the 𝑅 𝐴 -atoms in their root entries, the 

𝑐 ★-atoms in the parameter entry, which carries both modes exactly when the consume case charges both. A distinct-variable pair inhabits two distinct entries, so (sep-lock) on the frame’s [Ψ𝐴 , Φ𝐴 ]System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 59 

(Appendix C.4) followed by (sep-sc) on both sides ( (sc-elem) into the entries) pays it. Capture and type binders are the same computation with roots (Γ′, 𝐶 ∪ { 𝑐 }) = 𝑅 𝐴 ∪ { 𝑐 } and roots (Γ′, 𝐶 ) = 𝑅 𝐴 

respectively. 

Crossing into a continuation. Let the site be the continuation of a (let) with head charge 𝐶 1

and continuation charge 𝐶 2. Pairs within roots (Γ, 𝐶 2) are inherited: 𝐶 2 ⊆ 𝐶 1 ∪ 𝐶 2, and the paying derivations extend to the continuation’s context. They also survive the kill that the translated (let) 

or (unpack) applies: the killed variables are the consume -marked roots of the head’s translated charge, which Theorem C.16 (sequencing clause) on the source premise Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲ 𝐶 2 keeps out of the variables of roots (Γ, 𝐶 2), and a payment touches no authority beyond its two variables (Theorem C.17). For a fresh -carrying let, the continuation’s roots additionally contain the witness atoms 𝑐 𝑖 , consume 𝑐 𝑖 . A pair of witness atoms over distinct variables is paid by (sep-consumable) ,whose modes are unconstrained. A pair of a witness atom with an atom 𝜈 𝑞 of roots (Γ, 𝐶 2) is paid by the ownership lock [Ψ𝑤 , Φ𝑤 ] of the translated (unpack) : the translation instantiates the rule’s continuation slot at the root closure of the continuation’s use set (Appendix C.8), so Ψ𝑤 ’s two entries are the mode-closed witness tuple and a root-level set containing 𝜈 𝑞 ; (sep-lock) separates the entries and (sep-sc) descends to the two atoms. □

Corollary C.22 (Satisfaction discharge). At each translated elimination (Appendix C.5), the satisfaction obligation JΓK |= [𝜎 Ψ𝐴 , 𝜎 Φ𝐴 ] of the instantiated lock is derivable at the site. 

Proof. By canonicity (declared subjects) the lock is the one manufactured at the callee’s declared type, with entries the parameter entry, instantiated to J𝐷 K (at both modes for a consumer), and the root entries of 𝑅 𝐴 . The obligation is pairwise separation of the entries, plus the Φ legs. 

Root-entry pairs. Two root entries carry distinct variables 𝑝 ≠ 𝑞 of 𝑅 𝐴 by construction. Both belong to J𝜌 (𝑠 )K: the ⌊𝐶 ⌋-part of 𝑅 𝐴 equals roots (Γ, {𝑥 }) for the charged subject (declared annotation), and the ⌊𝐶 𝑇 ⌋-part is covered by roots (Γ, 𝐶 𝑦 ) = roots (Γ, {𝑦 }) by domain honesty (Appendix C.1). Theorem C.21 pays each atom pair, and (sep-union) with (sep-sc) assembles atoms into the entries. For (tapp) these are the only pairs, and no source premise is consumed, matching the rule, which has none. 

Witness pairs. A pair of the instantiated parameter entry 𝜇 J𝐷 K with a root entry over 𝑞 resolves upward (Theorem C.9) to atom pairs (𝜇 ′ 𝑑, 𝜈 𝑞 ) with 𝑑 a variable of roots (Γ, 𝐷 ). If 𝑑 ≠ 𝑞 , the pair is payable: 𝑑 lies in 𝜌 (𝑠 ) by tightness ( (app) ) or because the witness is charged ( (capp) , (consume-app) ), and 𝑞 as above. If 𝑑 = 𝑞 , the source separation premise Γ ⊢ 𝐷 ⊲⊳ |𝐴 |, whose right side contains 

⌊𝐶 ∪ 𝐶 𝑇 ⌋ and hence resolves onto 𝑅 𝐴 , makes both atoms read-only by Theorem C.16, and (sep-ro) 

pays the singleton pair as in Theorem C.18. (sep-union) , (sep-symm) , and (sep-sc) assemble the atoms and descend to the entries. 

Mode legs. Φ𝐴 is empty except at an ro -bounded capture binder, where the obligation after 

[𝑐 := J𝐷 K] is ⊢ J𝐷 K : ro , the translated image through Theorem C.12 of the kinding Γ ⊢ 𝐷 : ro that 

(sb-kind) established when the source narrowed the bound to 𝐷 . □

Remark C.2 (Ownership is paid, not decreed). The continuation case of Theorem C.21 rests on the ownership lock that (unpack) manufactures; this remark records why the rule carries it and why its plain sequencing premise suffices to pay for it. Core (sep-consumable) separates two distinct consumable roots, but the continuation also needs separations between an owned root and older 

bindings: minimally, with 𝑇 𝑎 , rp , and alloc as in Appendix C.9, an access-only abstraction root against a fresh result bound later in the same body, 𝑓 = 𝜆 (𝑜𝑝 : 𝑇 𝑎 ). let 𝑓 𝑟𝑒𝑠ℎ = alloc () in rp 𝑜𝑝 𝑓 𝑟𝑒𝑠ℎ ,whose source derivation uses Γ ⊢ { 𝑜𝑝 } ⊲⊳ {𝑓 𝑟𝑒𝑠ℎ }. No fiat ownership rule can supply these: an axiom separating a ⊤-bounded consume root from everything older conflates the root’s binding time with its footprint’s provenance : an unpack witness is young as a binding , but its footprint is the 60 Xu et al. 

consumed evidence’s, inherited verbatim, and an older binding may alias it. With consume 𝑐 𝑎 <:

⊤, 𝑎 : Ref [𝑇 ] ∧ {𝑐 𝑎 } in scope and 𝑐 𝑎 live, 

𝜆 [𝑐 𝑖 <: ⊤] 𝜆 (𝑔 : Ref [𝑇 ] ∧ {𝑐 𝑖 }) let ⟨𝑐 𝑗 , 𝑥 ⟩ = ⟨{ 𝑐 𝑎 }, 𝑎 ⟩ in 𝑡 

satisfies both natural guards ( 𝑐 𝑗 is ⊤-bounded, 𝑐 𝑖 is older), yet (capp) may instantiate 𝑐 𝑖 := {𝑐 𝑎 },an access-only view of the still-live source that the kill at the unpack does not remove; the two “separate” sides share 𝑐 𝑎 ’s cell. The mechanization refuted exactly this rule and its ownership-at-birth invariant; freshness-at-creation is a fact about (alloc) , not about unpacking. Ownership is instead a paid certificate , in the same way the function locks of Appendix C.3 pay for their parameter separations: (unpack) manufactures the lock Ψ𝑤 from what its own premises prove. The payment is the footprint model’s witness-confinement bound : every location reachable from a pack’s witness evidence is either covered at consume mode by the producing computation’s charge 𝐶 1, or allocated during that computation. A fresh location cannot lie in the continuation charge’s footprint, live before the computation runs; and a 𝐶 1-consume-covered location shared with 𝐶 2’s footprint is a consume-then-use conflict, which is precisely what Γ ⊢ 𝐶 1 ⊲ 𝐶 2 denies: its access-only leg denotes a consume-free charge, forcing every witness fresh, and its separating leg denies the overlap outright. In particular the plain sequencing premise suffices; a strengthened separation premise, which an earlier revision adopted after refuting a discharge of the lock through the premise’s separation semantics alone (a fact about that discharge route, not about the rule), is unnecessary, and would forbid a continuation from re-touching an access-shared producer, e.g. calling the same existential-returning function twice. Two aspects of how the lock is instantiated 

matter to Theorem C.21. The witness entry is stored at both access modes: the confinement bound is a fact about the witnesses’ locations, indifferent to the mode at which the continuation later touches them, and the consume -marked reading is what pays the continuation’s own consumption of a witness against its remaining charge. The continuation entry is stored in root-resolved form, chosen by the translation when it instantiates the rule; a rule-level root enrichment would instead strictly enlarge the recorded footprint and demand a genuinely stronger premise. All of this is mechanized: the refutations, the lock-manufacturing (unpack) as the sole unpack rule of the development, and the headline theorems (the fundamental theorem, adequacy, immutability, standardization, and confluence), which check with no axioms beyond propositional extensionality, choice, and quotient soundness. 

L10: Kill transport. The core (let) and (unpack) type their continuation in the killed context 

Γ ⊖𝐶 1, whereas the induction produces the translated continuation in the unkilled JΓK. The bridge is that translated derivations consult consume authority only at charged roots, which sequencing keeps live. 

Definition C.23 (Authority robustness). A CoreCapybara derivation is authority-robust for a set 𝑋 

of capture variables when every leaf that consults a binding’s consume authority, an ⊢ · accessible 

premise, a ⊢ · consumable premise, or a (sep-consumable) instance, mentions only capture variables that are in 𝑋 or bound within the derivation itself. ( (sc-cvar) also reads a binding, but applies only to access-only bindings, which no kill targets, so it needs no tracking; (k-imm) and 

(sep-lock) read locks, not authority.) 

Lemma C.24 (Kill transport). Let 𝐶 ; Γ ⊢ 𝑡 : 𝐸 in CoreCapybara by a derivation authority-robust for 𝑋 , and let no variable killed by Γ ⊖ 𝐶 1 belong to 𝑋 . Then 𝐶 ; Γ ⊖ 𝐶 1 ⊢ 𝑡 : 𝐸 , by a derivation authority-robust for the same 𝑋 ; and likewise for every auxiliary judgment. 

Proof. By induction on the derivation. The kill rewrites consume authorities and nothing else: every payload, every lock entry, and every type is unchanged, so each rule that does not consult System Capybara: Tracking Capabilities for Separation and Freshness 61 

authority re-applies verbatim on the inductive hypotheses. The authority-consulting leaves survive because their variables are in 𝑋 or derivation-local, hence not killed: an ⊢ · accessible premise finds no killed binding among them, a ⊢ · consumable premise and a (sep-consumable) instance find their consume bindings intact, and (sc-cvar) reads access-only bindings, which the kill never touches. □

The main induction produces derivations that are authority-robust for 𝑋 𝑠 = J𝜌 (𝑠 )K, the translated site root set: every elimination’s subject is charged by the source (surface (var) charges occurrences eagerly), every consumable premise concerns a charged or witness set, and every (sep-consumable) 

instance introduced by Theorems C.18 to C.21 pairs atoms of 𝜌 (𝑠 ). The let case of Appendix C.8 verifies that the killed roots avoid exactly this set. 

C.8 Proof of the Translation Theorem 

We prove Theorem C.4 by induction on the canonical source derivation, one case per rule. Through-out, 𝐶 ′ denotes the translated use set, verified root-covered by J𝐶 K; unless stated, the translated result type is J𝑇 K∃ by construction. Three recurring facts are used without further comment. 

Stamping : whenever roots (JΓK, 𝐶 ′) ⊑ 𝑊 for a root-level capture set 𝑊 , also JΓK ⊢ 𝐶 ′ <: 𝑊 ,by Theorem C.9 followed by (sc-elem) , (sc-mode) , and (sc-union) on the covering; this is what matches a translated body charge against the stated annotation 𝑊 𝐴 and a translated use set against a root-closure slot. Robustness : each case’s derivation is authority-robust for J𝜌 (𝑠 )K (Theorem C.23), by inspection of its leaves. Consumed charges : every consume -marked atom of a translated use set either belongs to a translated (pack) , (consumer-app) , (dealloc) , or (unpack) charge, each guarded by a consumable premise translated through Theorem C.12, or resolves from an annotation stamped from such a charge, so its variable is consume -bound.

State, parallelism, and conditionals. (alloc) , (write) , (dealloc) , and (if) map to their core name-sakes with the premises translated by Theorem C.12; (read) inserts the reader as in Appendix C.5, its administrative let sequencing by (seq-access-only) (a reader value charges nothing). (par)

C.9 Example: runParallel 

We trace the runParallel pattern of Section 2 through the translation, exercising the lock manufacture of Appendix C.3 and the satisfaction discharge of Theorem C.22. Use a type variable 𝑋 (declared 

𝑋 <: ⊤) for the resource shape, take Unit and () as a base type and its value as in the core calculus, and abbreviate 𝑇 𝑎 = 𝑋 ∧ {any }, a resource whose capture is a fresh any . Take 

𝑇 rp = ∀( 𝑜𝑝 1 : 𝑇 𝑎 )  (∀( 𝑜𝑝 2 : 𝑇 𝑎 )Unit ) ∧ {𝑜𝑝 1 },

the curried type of runParallel : applied to 𝑜𝑝 1 it returns a closure that has captured 𝑜𝑝 1 and awaits

The outer lock Ψ1 has a single entry, the parameter root: the outer arrow’s annotation is empty, so 𝑅 𝐴 1 = {} , and a one-entry lock demands no pairs; its satisfaction is vacuous. (Theorem C.16) and payable by the ambient invariant (Theorem C.21), here through the consume authority of the two unpacked roots. The manufactured lock thus rejects exactly the racy call, as Section 2 requires.
